VISUAL RECORDS - GIGAS

[BEGIN LOG.]

[Agent Vaughan approaches Agent Xob. They are on opposing ends of the central chamber. There is what appears to be a large well in the middle of the room between them. He raises his blade and points it at her.]

[Agent Xob narrows her eyes, looking confused. Movement of camera indicates that Agent Vaughan is telling her something. He appears to wait for her to respond.]

[Agent Xob looks around, and appears to ask a question. Agent Vaughan replies, appearing to gesticulate wildly for 5 seconds.]

[Agent Xob begins to smile incredulously. Agent Vaughan appears to shout something.]

[Agent Xob waves her arms around exasperatedly, gesturing at Agent Vaughan. At one or two points, she appears to mock Agent Vaughan's mannerism. After 20 seconds, she ceases.]

[Agent Xob stares at Agent Vaughan, and speaks for 3 minutes and 26 seconds. Agent Vaughan appears to grow more distressed over the course of this duration. Agent Xob's emotion does not change over this period of time.]

[Agent Xob is silent for a few seconds, then, she steps on the edge of the well. Agent Vaughan rushes to draw his automatic and points it at her, then points to the floor, apparently gesturing for her to get down.]

[Agent Xob chuckles, before jumping into the well. Agent Vaughan rushes to the edge and peers down. The well is completely pitch black.]

[Agent Vaughan stares down the well for 1 minute and 43 seconds. When he starts moving again, camera movement suggests that he is shaking.]

[END LOG.]

Closing Note: After REDSIGHT team arrived at the location of interest, the well inside the central chamber was checked again several times.

The well was four foot deep, and was found to contain nothing inside.




















A Light In The Dark

"Something where there should be nothing."

You don’t really remember for how long you’ve been swimming through the dark, and frankly you were content with that. In all honesty, you stopped counting long ago. You were okay with the prospect of simply floating here forever in the void.

Mind over matter, you thought to yourself.

You’d chosen the darkness, and there really was no question in if it was the right thing to do, because it was. It was the only thing to do, and in this dark place where no god can see, that thought comforted you enough to deal with everything else.

Somewhere out there, things are better.

At one point, you forgot if you were you, as weightless and massless as you were, or if you were your shadow. The fact that most of your limbs had disintegrated and gone to mush by then didn’t help. Shortly after, you decided to stop differentiating between the two.

Somewhere out there, the world got better, just as soon as I stopped looking.

You wondered if you were dead, now that the dark had taken all the pieces of you that it could, and whether if the transition had happened so quietly and seamlessly that you didn’t even notice at all. Hey, if you didn’t notice, who’s to say that you haven’t been dead all this time? Maybe you weren’t even alive in the first place. Something to think about. Pile it with all the others.

Somewhere out there, I met you before all the bad stuff that happened to us all.

So one of these days, you felt a presence.

And it was a jarring experience, the sensation of a being that wasn’t your own. An experience from a past you’d left behind long ago. And before you knew it, an utterance emerged from the throat that you didn’t know you still had, echoing through the void into ears that you believed to be gone.

“Who’s there?”

A silence fills your world as the noise subsides. A silence more profound than any that you’ve experienced since you came here. A wait that felt like it lasted for an eternity, and maybe it did, before-

“Nobody.”

You paused.

”Well, you have to be somebody. I’m talking to you.”

“Mm. I guess that’s true.”

And the other party falls silent. You look around, but you still can’t find them, so you try to reach around, thrusting the hands you didn’t have into the surrounding aether.

“Yes, yes, I can see you. Hello.”

You feel a gust of wind - or perhaps just some force - rippling through the air, as if some great beast had waved back in response. Some parts of your memories begin to come to the surface. Bright, white eyes in the dark. Sharpened teeth to gnaw at the flesh.

The things that can see in the dark.

”…Excuse me?”

“Yes?”

”…Do you happen to be… a cat?”

“No, I don’t think so.”

”Oh, good.”

“Why do you ask?”

”I don't like cats.”

And the two of you were silent again, but you can sense the not-cat slowly drift towards you. A smell like iron, or dust, or old book wafts towards you, and it somehow escapes your notice that you now had your nose back.

”Well, if you’re not a cat, then what are you?”

“Good question.”

More silence. You suddenly feel more tired than you've ever felt. You stretch your neck and there is a crack.

“I was a machine. Or a part of it. A thing that did what it was told that it had to do. And every day, I fulfilled my purpose to the best that I could. I picked up the little people, I pulled them apart, all the tiny little details, and I put them into the machine. I did it for so long, and I was so good at it. Tiny pests, small creatures, I crushed them all beneath steel fangs.”

You narrow lidless eyes. You scratched your chin with re-emerging fingers.

”Sounds like a cat to me.”

And then the other thing laughed without a sound.

“Maybe. Maybe that’s why I’m here. But don’t worry, I don’t do that anymore. Down here, I’m just someone passing by. Down here, I’m just someone who’s doing the best that he can, looking for other lost souls. Some who answers to a higher calling.”

”A higher calling?”

“Something lies deeper down in the darkness below us. Something large and shifting and writhing and living. I was once like you, you know. Cold, rotting, dying in the dark. I know what it feels like to be deconstructed. To be disassembled and put back wrong.”

The air grows cold on your skin. It continues to approach.

”…I don’t understand. Why are you here? Why did you come to me?”

“Are you really happy with the way things went, Hannah?”

A pause. Whatever remained of you (there's more than you expected) shifts uncomfortably.

”…Who are you?”

“Well, are you? Are you satisfied with the ways things ended? Is it enough for you to believe that everything will be alright?”

Chills run down your spine. You have a spine. Thoughts rushes through your head as you feel yourself becoming more alert every second, long-dead chemical processes restarts as your sinew knits itself together. The thing in the dark gets closer.

”What do you want?”

“I lost my light, long ago. And all there was left to do was to atone. So many years, so empty, so alone. And then… It found me.”

”I said, what do you want?”

“To help you. To reach out. It healed me, as it can heal you. It gave me back my light…”

And then it appeared before you. Just in front of your face. The first flash of color that you can remember in this dreamless sleep. It pulsated and glowed and emanated silent judgement.

A single blinking red light.

“…as it can give you back yours, too.”

You saw yourself in the red glow. Everything was back where it should be. Everything was as it should be. And you knew the catch. You knew it could all go away again. You knew…

”…and if I say no?”

“It’s your choice.”

And in the end, it really was. So you thought to yourself if it was really enough, and decided it wasn’t, and you swore the red blinking light came a bit closer, and closer, and closer, almost imperceptibly. And you knew what came next, and maybe it’ll be better. Maybe it’ll be okay this time.

And he said he wasn’t a cat…

”Okay.”

“Reach out. It doesn’t take anything more than that.”

And you do, you reach out towards the red dot… and, seizing the opportunity, lunge forward to grab onto the barely-visible shifting mass behind it.

No, not a cat, you thought to yourself. Anglerfish.

And another second passes, and you’re clinging to something bony and skeletal and wiry, and there is screaming in a multitude of voices, and you don’t know how you’re still alive, or why, or where you are, because your world is being dragged towards the light that grows ever bigger on the horizons. You don’t know where you’re going, you don’t know what’s going to happen.

All you know is that

you’re

not

going

up.

False Start

"You were made for this."

He jolts awake, gasping in cold sweat, adrenaline thundering through his veins. He was shivering. His clothes were completely drenched.

It was another one of these nights, like countless others, and yet, still, he never got quite used to it. The blood, the horrors, the images of red lights in the sky. Of a billion bodies smeared across the street like paste. It was natural, with what he’s gone through. He just needed to accept that some fundamental part of him was broken, and that this was how it’ll always be.

He got up, opened the wardrobe, and retrieved a fresh set of sleeping clothes. He swore under his breath as the creak of the door echoed through the room. He thought that was fixed by now.

“Bad dream again?” murmured the woman on the other side of the bed. He didn’t nod because she couldn’t see him from this angle anyways.

He downed half a bottle of water along with his medicine, and pressed his head against the window, just trying to ride it out.

“Bad entire fucking life.” He muttered under his breath. When he turned around, she was already fast asleep again. How does it come so easily to some people?

It doesn’t matter. He had an important meeting tomorrow. Gotta put all the worries out of his mind, quick. Gotta bring his A-game in just 5 more hours. Gotta go to sleep again, because if he didn’t, things would fall apart, just like that. You’ve gone through this night after night before, you can handle this.

And yet, that night, for some reason that escaped him entirely, the dread in his stomach did not subside, and Dr. Robert Montauk simply stared at the ceiling until the sun came up - trying to ignore the growing red spot in the back of his mind, the writhing beneath his false skin, the emptiness that had begun to drip into his being.

The Montauk Machine - The End.

Filename: ForestCenter.png

Author: FrankEntropy

Footnotes
1. The Brightspot program was a Foundation recruitment initiative created in 1951 in collaboration with the American government.
2. Crohnon’s Problem (abolished 1980 due to a lack of focus on Ethical standards) was a philosophical assignment developed by the Foundation Department Of Recruitment in order to assess potential Foundation recruits. The examinee is asked to develop a philosophical framework as well as practical policies and measures to suppress the existence of a random emerging global anomalous phenomenon. A score above 94 was a prerequisite for applicants of the Brightspot scholarship.
3. Precursors to the Foundation’s current line of Akiva counters.
4. Further details on the Malfeasance Crisis and Dr. Russell’s involvement cannot be divulged aside from what has been written here under the 1982 Harmful Intelligence Directive
5. A Hume is a unit of measurement that measures how much reality is in a given area. Rapid Hume shifts can cause destabilization of local reality.
6. Information on operating SCP-9317-B is available to the SCP-9317 Operation Team.
7. "Akiva radiation refers to fluctuations in the anomalous field responsible for interactions between belief and reality" -Foundation Akiva Counter Operating Instructions.
8. Further information on SCP-9317-D is restricted to the SCP-9317 Maintenance Team.
9. It is suspected that this is one of the primary factors leading to SCP-9317 becoming damaged prior to recovery.
10. Kraterocracy - Rule by the strong; a system of governance where those who are strong enough to seize power through physical force, social maneuvering or political cunning.
11. Social Darwinism - A body of pseudoscientific theories and societal practices that purport to apply biological concepts of natural selection and survival of the fittest to sociology, economics and politics.
12. "Anarcho-Primitivism" - An anarchist critique of civilization that advocates a return to non-civilized ways of life through deindustrialization, abolition of the division of labor or specialization, abandonment of large-scale organization and all technology other than prehistoric technology, and the dissolution of agriculture.

18. It is believed that the Vatican currently possesses nearly all information pertaining to Da'vo Christianity.
19. The true extent of Da'vo Christianity’s involvement in shaping modern Christianity is unknown, as the Church would later order extensive cover-ups and purges in an attempt to remove all knowledge of Da'vo Christianity from the public knowledge. Similarly unknown is the fate of the Da'vo Christian population.
